## 1. Multilingual AI in Universities - Advancing Inclusion Through UA and Stakeholder Insights

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 09:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | West Wing Room No. 6 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Sameer Gahlot, National Internet Exchange of India |
| ü§ù **Partners** | National Internet Exchange of India |

> As digital technologies become central to education, linguistic accessibility emerges as a critical equity issue.. This study examines how universities enable multilingual participation through UA.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

As digital technologies become central to education, linguistic accessibility emerges as a critical equity issue. This study examines how universities enable multilingual participation through UA. Drawing on Diffusion Innovation Theory (DIT) and Technology Acceptance Model (TAM), this investigation reviews stakeholder experiences across universities in Asia and Europe using an innovative AI-assisted interview methodology. The findings also revealed critical gaps in universities' capacity to advance UN SDG 4/9/10/17 through inclusive digital infrastructure while presenting billions of dollars opportunity.

</details>

---

## 2. Safe & Trusted AI at Scale

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 09:30 ‚Äì 10:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | L1 Meeting Room No. 14 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Arvind Kumar, STPI, Ashok Meena, Ministry of Jal Shakti, Dr . Piyush Singla, Govt of J&K, Dr Rajiv KN, BWSSB, Dr. Ravi Gupta, Elets Technomedia, Mohammed Safirulla, India AI Mission, Sid Sheth, d-MATRIX |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Elets Technomedia Pvt Ltd |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/ANrK8Ko6J-I?feature=share) |

> As AI adoption accelerates from isolated pilots to enterprise-wide integration, attention is shifting toward the creation of safe, trusted, and scalable ecosystems.. This high-impact session examines practical implementation frameworks, governance architectures, and leadership strategies that reconcile rapid innovation with accountability and risk management.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

As AI adoption accelerates from isolated pilots to enterprise-wide integration, attention is shifting toward the creation of safe, trusted, and scalable ecosystems. This high-impact session examines practical implementation frameworks, governance architectures, and leadership strategies that reconcile rapid innovation with accountability and risk management. The emphasis is on operationalising responsible AI in ways that deliver measurable outcomes while safeguarding security, regulatory compliance, and long-term resilience. By convening policymakers, industry leaders, and technology experts, the session advances a systems-level understanding of how AI can be deployed at scale to drive productivity, institutional trust, and inclusive growth in an increasingly AI-driven global economy.

</details>

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 09:30 ‚Äì 10:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | West Wing Room 4 B |

| ü§ù **Partners** | TIC Council (Headquarters- Brussels, Belgium) |

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

This roundtable convenes policymakers, regulators, industry leaders, and global experts to shape trusted pathways for AI adoption. It examines how AI-enabled Quality Infrastructure can strengthen governance, accountability, and global acceptance. Through applied use cases and international perspectives, it highlights interoperable assurance frameworks that reduce compliance friction, boost MSME competitiveness, enable cross-border trade, and position India as a leader in responsible, innovation-driven AI growth for inclusive, secure, and scalable digital transformation.

</details>

## 6. Culturally - Grounded AI: How Social Norms Can Inform AI 
Systems

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 09:30 ‚Äì 10:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | L1 Meeting Room No. 17 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Amita Yadav, Karya, Mohit Jain, PhD, Microsoft Research India, Bangalore, Philipp Zimmer, World Bank Group, Washington DC, Sharath Chandra Guntuku, PhD, University of Pennsylvania, School of Engineering and Applied Science, Sunny Rai, PhD, University of Pennsylvania, School of Engineering and Applied Science |
| ü§ù **Partners** | University of Pennsylvania |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/gcGuWLCNinQ?feature=share) |

> AI systems deployed across diverse cultural contexts often fail not because of technical limitations, but because they overlook social norms‚Äîthe unwritten rules that shape human behaviour and decision-making.. A recommendation system that succeeds in the United States may not resonate in India.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

AI systems deployed across diverse cultural contexts often fail not because of technical limitations, but because they overlook social norms‚Äîthe unwritten rules that shape human behaviour and decision-making. A recommendation system that succeeds in the United States may not resonate in India. A health chatbot that effectively engages American users may alienate Indian communities if it does not reflect local expectations and communication styles. This research-focused session convenes leading scholarship and applied work examining how culturally grounded design, local data partnerships, and participatory methods can improve AI performance across contexts. The emphasis is on embedding social understanding into model development to ensure effectiveness, legitimacy, and equitable impact across geographies.

</details>

The Panel Discussion will focus on short-term and long-term impact of AI on employment, both at the industry level (e.g., manufacturing, healthcare, automobile) and function level (e.g., HR, sales, supply chain). ## 20. Information Integrity as an Infrastructure for Trust: Empowering Youth and Future Generations

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 10:30 ‚Äì 11:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | West Wing Room 4 B |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Alpesh Shah, IEEE Standards Association (IEEE SA), Amir Banifatemi, AI Commons, Gabriela Ramos, IEEE, Karine Perset, OECD, Mariagrazia Squicciarini, Unesco, Mohammed Misbahuddin, C-DAC Bangalore, Moira Patterson, IEEE SA, Tanya Perelmuter, Fondation Abeona, Uyi Stewart, Inclusive Innovation & Analytics at Mastercard, Yuko Harayama, IEEE, Yuko Harayama, RIKEN in charge of international affairs |
| ü§ù **Partners** | IEEE |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/fYCRZhqSFT8?feature=share) |

> The proliferation of generative AI and algorithmic content systems has created a new kind of risk for young users globally: Increasing exposure to manipulative design, hyper-personalized content, and AI-generated information at an overwhelming scale.. Age-Appropriate Design (AAD) is a policy and design framework that helps develop safer, more accountable digital environments with the best interests of children in mind.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

The proliferation of generative AI and algorithmic content systems has created a new kind of risk for young users globally: Increasing exposure to manipulative design, hyper-personalized content, and AI-generated information at an overwhelming scale. Age-Appropriate Design (AAD) is a policy and design framework that helps develop safer, more accountable digital environments with the best interests of children in mind.

</details>

---

| | |
|---|---|

| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | West Wing Room No. 6 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Amba Kak, AI Now Institute, Augustine Peter, Competition Commission of India, Kush Amlani, Global Competition & Regulation, Mozilla, Payal Malik, Competitiion Commission of India, Shweta Rajpal Kohli, Startup Policy Forum (India) |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Mozilla |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/2_0hT-MZB4g?feature=share) |

> AI risks being shaped by a concentrated few, leaving the Global South as consumers rather than co-creators.. When data, compute, foundational models, and distribution are controlled by a handful of corporations, innovation suffers.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

AI risks being shaped by a concentrated few, leaving the Global South as consumers rather than co-creators. When data, compute, foundational models, and distribution are controlled by a handful of corporations, innovation suffers. A competitive, open source AI stack, built on affordable compute, local cloud options, and locally trained models, is essential to fostering innovation. This panel explores AI resource distribution, barriers facing Global South innovators, and remedies through openness, competition, and South‚ÄìSouth cooperation.

</details>

It will examine tradeoffs through case studies and practical examples, covering sovereign and open-source AI, compute infrastructure, DPI, and risks of dependency. The aim is to identify empirically grounded pathways that enable countries to pursue a "third way" toward technological autonomy in a challenging global environment.

| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/I2ulxdGlKvQ?feature=share) |

> Global policy discourse largely treats AI and DPI separately.. AI discussions focus on model safety, compute governance, workforce displacement.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

Global policy discourse largely treats AI and DPI separately. AI discussions focus on model safety, compute governance, workforce displacement. DPI conversations center on digital identity, digital payment, data exchange. AI-DPI convergence can create exponential value and new risk categories. While this convergence accelerates, critical questions remain: How can DPI lower barriers for local AI innovation while preventing new forms of exclusion? How can responsible AI systems be built in resource-constrained environments using DPI approaches?

</details>

## 126. Towards Global Cooperation for Equitable AI in Healthcare

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 17:30 ‚Äì 18:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | L1 Meeting Room No. 14 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Dr. Krithika Rangaranjan, AIIMS, New Delhi, Dr. Mahima Kalla, Centre for Digital Transformation of Health, University of Melbourne, Dr. Mahima Kalla, Centre for Digital Transformation of Health, University of Melbourne, Mr. Aman Taneja, Ikigai Law, Mr. Aman Taneja, Ikigai Law, Mr. Mohit Jain, Microsoft India, Ms. Kanika Kalra, World Health Organization, Ms. Tess Buckley, techUK |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Centre for Digital Transformation of Health (CDTH), The University of Melbourne |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/QxHpG6qU4OY?feature=share) |

> Artificial Intelligence (AI) promises to transform healthcare delivery worldwide, improving diagnostics, access, and system efficiency.. Yet biased datasets, exclusionary design choices, and uneven deployment risk reinforcing inequities and disproportionately harming already marginalised communities, including the elderly, persons with disabilities, and rural populations.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

Artificial Intelligence (AI) promises to transform healthcare delivery worldwide, improving diagnostics, access, and system efficiency. Yet biased datasets, exclusionary design choices, and uneven deployment risk reinforcing inequities and disproportionately harming already marginalised communities, including the elderly, persons with disabilities, and rural populations. This interdisciplinary panel will explore inclusive AI strategies, such as participatory design, representative data practices, and context-sensitive governance frameworks, to ensure that AI systems in healthcare are designed, developed, and deployed in ways that mitigate unintended harm. The focus is on building equitable digital health ecosystems that proactively address structural disparities rather than amplify them.

</details>

As AI moves beyond language, new foundation models are emerging that predict, design, and translate materials into manufacturable processes. This panel brings together academia, industry, and infrastructure partners to discuss physics-focused foundational models, their responsible applications in biology, energy, and manufacturing, and the national strategies needed for sovereign capability. Attendees will see a live Physics model demo, explore technical and ethical challenges, policy frameworks, and map pathways for industrial validation, pilot deployment, and collaborative scaling.

</details>

| ü§ù **Partners** | BharatGen, TIH for IoT & IoE, IIT Bombay. |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/1b-sjb-L-ig?feature=share) |

> The flagship Param2 17B-parameter sovereign multilingual foundation model has been built fully in India using a Mixture-of-Experts architecture.. It supports 22 Indian languages and is trained on large India-centric datasets developed under Data lakes.
Alongside advanced text models, sovereign AI capabilities are being expanded across speech models in 12 languages as well as document vision models.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

The flagship Param2 17B-parameter sovereign multilingual foundation model has been built fully in India using a Mixture-of-Experts architecture. It supports 22 Indian languages and is trained on large India-centric datasets developed under Data lakes.
Alongside advanced text models, sovereign AI capabilities are being expanded across speech models in 12 languages as well as document vision models. The event will also showcase deployment-ready platforms designed for governance, healthcare, education, finance, and cultural preservation.

</details>

| ü§ù **Partners** | Nasscom |

> From AI-generated content and code to foundation models, traditional boundaries of authorship, inventorship, and ownership are increasingly contested as jurisdictions adapt their intellectual property regimes.. <details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

From AI-generated content and code to foundation models, traditional boundaries of authorship, inventorship, and ownership are increasingly contested as jurisdictions adapt their intellectual property regimes. The IndiaAI Mission positions indigenous datasets, models, and compute infrastructure as strategic national assets for innovation, exports, and long-term economic growth. Without a future-ready AI‚ÄìIP framework, India risks legal uncertainty that could constrain innovation and investment. This session situates AI‚ÄìIP policy within the vision of Viksit Bharat, linking science and innovation, safe and trusted AI, and AI-led economic growth and social good.

</details>

capture and learn from them remains fragmented. This session brings together policymakers, and

warning, and coordinated response. Participants will discuss institutional designs ‚Äîfrom shared taxonomies to secure 
data-sharing‚Äîthat can turn incident data into actionable governance, standards, and risk-management insights.

## 375. Sovereign AI Infrastructure for Bharat and Global South

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 11:30 ‚Äì 12:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Sushma Swaraj Bhawan | Shakuntalam Banquet |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Abhishek Upperwal, Soket AI Labs, Neelakantan Venkataraman, Tata Communications, Rachel Adams, Global Center on AI Governance, Ravinder Kumar, Tecnod8.ai, Sourav Bandyopadhyay, Shunya Labs, Srikanth Velamakanni, Fractal Analytics Limited, Tarun Dua, E2E Networks Limited |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Nasscom |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/7wx8yIouJ28?feature=share) |

> India's strategic AI infrastructure must be built around three core pillars: security, sustainability, and open standards.. Aligned with the objectives of Atmanirbhar Bharat and Digital Personal Data Protection (DPDP) compliance, this session examines the emerging architecture of sovereign compute ecosystems, including edge‚Äìcloud convergence for next-generation (6G) networks, neuromorphic computing, and low-precision inference systems designed for scalable deployment.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

India's strategic AI infrastructure must be built around three core pillars: security, sustainability, and open standards. Aligned with the objectives of Atmanirbhar Bharat and Digital Personal Data Protection (DPDP) compliance, this session examines the emerging architecture of sovereign compute ecosystems, including edge‚Äìcloud convergence for next-generation (6G) networks, neuromorphic computing, and low-precision inference systems designed for scalable deployment. It further explores multi-agent orchestration frameworks and cross-sector compute-exchange models that can expand access to high-performance computing for startups, academia, and public institutions. Such an approach aims to democratise advanced computational resources while strengthening India's long-term digital sovereignty, innovation capacity, and research acceleration.

</details>

## 393. AI for Energy Systems/Utilities

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 12:30 ‚Äì 13:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | L1 Meeting Room No. 9 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Srikanth Kodali, Nvidia |
| ü§ù **Partners** | NVIDIA |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/g3dt2Rjp9OA?feature=share) |

> Amid rising energy demands from AI data centers, renewables, and electrification, utilities and energy firms grapple with grid stability, predictive maintenance, and subsurface uncertainties.. This NVIDIA speaker session unveils accelerated AI platforms - like Jetson for edge AI, Omniverse digital twins, and Grace Hopper Superchips - that revolutionize power utilities and upstream exploration.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

Amid rising energy demands from AI data centers, renewables, and electrification, utilities and energy firms grapple with grid stability, predictive maintenance, and subsurface uncertainties. This NVIDIA speaker session unveils accelerated AI platforms - like Jetson for edge AI, Omniverse digital twins, and Grace Hopper Superchips - that revolutionize power utilities and upstream exploration. Key highlights include generative AI for real-time grid management, EV integration, and battery optimization, alongside subsurface breakthroughs: NVIDIA-powered seismic processing for fault detection in 3D models, physics-informed neural networks (PhysicsNeMo) for reservoir simulations, NLP/LLMs integrating well logs/seismic data with partners like Shell and Saudi Aramco, and high-performance imaging via collaborations with SLB and Shearwater for CO2 storage and production forecasting. Attendees will explore the latest strides NVIDIA is making to improve energy efficiency (tokens per watt per dollar), accelerate simulations, reduce emissions, and optimize workflows from exploration to delivery - enabling a more resilient, low-carbon energy ecosystem. 

</details>

---

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

Climate change requires scalable AI solutions for mitigation, adaptation, and resilience. GPU-accelerated computing and AI are transforming high-resolution modeling, predictive analytics, and decision support for weather & climate applications. This session highlights NVIDIA‚Äôs Earth-2 and Omniverse. Earth-2 builds digital twins with observational and simulation data, open AI models, and a full software stack for forecasting, data assimilation, and informatics. Omniverse enables interactive visualization for scenario exploration. Applications span disaster preparedness, risk assessment, urban resilience, renewables, and sustainability -- delivering faster, cost-effective insights for real-world impact.

## 415. Masterclass on Democratizing Enterprise AI for Scale and Accuracy (Intellect Design Arena)

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 14:00 ‚Äì 15:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam - Expo Area | Hall No. 5 First Floor - Conference Room 1 |

 |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Intellect Design Arena |

> As India accelerates its journey toward becoming a global AI powerhouse, the transition from "experimental AI" to "enterprise-grade AI" remains a critical hurdle.. While Generative AI offers transformative potential, the primary barriers to adoption, within governance and business sectors, remain trust, governance, and accuracy.
This Master Class is designed to bridge the gap between the raw potential of AI and its practical, secure implementation, moving past the hype to address the "latent force" of enterprise-ready technology.
Guided by the Sutras of Progress, Impact, and Trust, the session provides a strategic roadmap for "Democratizing AI." This approach ensures advanced intelligence is no longer confined to data science labs but becomes accessible and scalable across all levels of an organization.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

As India accelerates its journey toward becoming a global AI powerhouse, the transition from "experimental AI" to "enterprise-grade AI" remains a critical hurdle. While Generative AI offers transformative potential, the primary barriers to adoption, within governance and business sectors, remain trust, governance, and accuracy.
This Master Class is designed to bridge the gap between the raw potential of AI and its practical, secure implementation, moving past the hype to address the "latent force" of enterprise-ready technology.
Guided by the Sutras of Progress, Impact, and Trust, the session provides a strategic roadmap for "Democratizing AI." This approach ensures advanced intelligence is no longer confined to data science labs but becomes accessible and scalable across all levels of an organization. By aligning the 7 Chakras of the Enterprise‚Äîfrom foundational Infrastructure to Strategy and Innovation‚Äîan organization evolves into a Cognitive Enterprise, where institutional wisdom is a shared resource and every individual is empowered to solve high-value problems.

</details>

## 473. Masterclass on Democratizing Enterprise AI for Scale and Accuracy (Intellect Design Arena)

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 15:30 ‚Äì 17:00 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam - Expo Area | Hall No. 4 First Floor - Conference Room 2 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Mr Arun Jain, Chairman & Founder of Intellect Design Arena and Chief Architect of Purple Fabric

 |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Intellect Design Arena |

> As India accelerates its journey toward becoming a global AI powerhouse, the transition from "experimental AI" to "enterprise-grade AI" remains a critical hurdle.. While Generative AI offers transformative potential, the primary barriers to adoption, within governance and business sectors, remain trust, governance, and accuracy.
This Master Class is designed to bridge the gap between the raw potential of AI and its practical, secure implementation, moving past the hype to address the "latent force" of enterprise-ready technology.
Guided by the Sutras of Progress, Impact, and Trust, the session provides a strategic roadmap for "Democratizing AI." This approach ensures advanced intelligence is no longer confined to data science labs but becomes accessible and scalable across all levels of an organization.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

As India accelerates its journey toward becoming a global AI powerhouse, the transition from "experimental AI" to "enterprise-grade AI" remains a critical hurdle. While Generative AI offers transformative potential, the primary barriers to adoption, within governance and business sectors, remain trust, governance, and accuracy.
This Master Class is designed to bridge the gap between the raw potential of AI and its practical, secure implementation, moving past the hype to address the "latent force" of enterprise-ready technology.
Guided by the Sutras of Progress, Impact, and Trust, the session provides a strategic roadmap for "Democratizing AI." This approach ensures advanced intelligence is no longer confined to data science labs but becomes accessible and scalable across all levels of an organization. By aligning the 7 Chakras of the Enterprise‚Äîfrom foundational Infrastructure to Strategy and Innovation‚Äîan organization evolves into a Cognitive Enterprise, where institutional wisdom is a shared resource and every individual is empowered to solve high-value problems.

</details>

| | |

For the users of the IndiaAI compute portal and the broader ecosystem, the selection of Graphics Processing Units (GPUs) has evolved from a simple metric of peak floating-point performance (FLOPS) into a complex optimization challenge involving memory bandwidth, interconnect topology, and architectural specialization.

The proliferation of Generative AI, driven by the advent of Large Language Models (LLMs), Visual Language Models (VLMs), and Agentic workflows, has fundamentally transformed the requirements for high-performance computing infrastructure. For the users of the IndiaAI compute portal and the broader ecosystem, the selection of Graphics Processing Units (GPUs) has evolved from a simple metric of peak floating-point performance (FLOPS) into a complex optimization challenge involving memory bandwidth, interconnect topology, and architectural specialization.

</details>

## 508. GIZ Policy Report & Developer Toolkit Launch (Hosted by Bhashini)

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 10:00 ‚Äì 11:00 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam - Expo Area | Hall No. 3 First Floor - Conference Room 4 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | K S Vishwanathan, DSCI
, Suket Amin, Sunbots
, Padmashree Shagrithaya |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Bhashini |

> This session marks the formal launch of a Policy Report and Developer's Toolkit prepared
in collaboration with GIZ and international partners.. The launch reflects growing global
cooperation in advancing multilingual AI and open digital ecosystems.
The policy report outlines strategic approaches for building inclusive language technologies,
while the developer toolkit provides practical resources to enable innovators, startups, and
public agencies to integrate multilingual AI capabilities into applications.
Participation of the German delegation highlights international interest in India's language
DPI model and opportunities for cross-country collaboration in AI governance, research, and
technology deployment.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

## 510. Future of AI DataCenter

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 10:00 ‚Äì 11:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam - Expo Area | Hall No. 4 First Floor - Conference Room 3 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Aadit Shah , Director - Velankani Information system PVT LTD

, Vibhor Iyer , Design Head- Velankani Information system PVT LTD |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Velankani Information System Pvt Ltd |

> AI workloads are driving explosive growth in data center power density‚Äîracks now routinely hit 100+ kW (vs.. traditional 10‚Äì20 kW), with megawatt-scale clusters and facilities demanding hundreds of MW.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

AI workloads are driving explosive growth in data center power density‚Äîracks now routinely hit 100+ kW (vs. traditional 10‚Äì20 kW), with megawatt-scale clusters and facilities demanding hundreds of MW. Power demand from global data centers is projected to rise 50‚Äì165% by 2030, largely due to AI.

The AI era is forcing a fundamental redesign‚Äînative HVDC distribution + liquid cooling will make high-density, sustainable AI infrastructure possible at scale, dramatically cutting losses, material use, and operational costs compared to legacy designs. The transition is already underway among hyperscalers and will become standard within 3‚Äì5 years.

Velankani Group is a leader in making Indigenous AI Data Center Infrastructure which will cater the demand for the Future.

</details>

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

The escalating frequency & intensity of climate related disasters present an existential threat to communities worldwide. AI offers a transformative, untapped potential to revolutionize EWS by processing massive datasets, enhancing predictive accuracy and accelerating warning dissemination. 
With India being a global pioneer in AI, leveraging its vast data and diverse talent pool, this session during the India AI Summit, calls for accelerated integration of AI to bridge technology adoption gap, ensuring disaster resilience for all.

</details>

multilingual service delivery at scale.

barriers.

> As AI evolves, the shift from centralized cloud computing to edge AI is transforming how data is processed and acted upon.. <details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

As AI evolves, the shift from centralized cloud computing to edge AI is transforming how data is processed and acted upon. By moving intelligence closer to data sources such as sensors, mobile devices, and IoT systems, edge AI reduces latency, bandwidth usage, and energy consumption while improving real-time decision-making, privacy, and security. Real-world applications will be highlighted along with emerging lightweight and generative AI models designed for resource-constrained edge environments.

</details>

> AI impact depends not on pilots, but on sustained adoption across institutions.. While innovation is abundant, diffusion capacity remains limited, leaving organizations to repeat costly experiments.

This session introduces AI Diffusion Infrastructure as a shared foundation of standards, playbooks, and trusted pathways that reduce operational and compliance risks. Leaders from technology, government, and development will explore how to scale safe, repeatable AI systems across sectors and geographies, turning isolated successes into equitable population scale outcomes.

As AI adoption accelerates, enterprises are assessing how the next wave of transformation differs from earlier expectations. This session brings together investors, founders, and transformation leaders to examine where enterprise AI can create value, where limitations remain, and how organisations can move from pilot initiatives to scaled deployment. The discussion will also consider how operating models may evolve in response to emerging AI-enabled workflows.

</details>

## 681. Enterprise-Grade Responsible AI for India and the Global South

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 17:30 ‚Äì 18:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Sushma Swaraj Bhawan | Nalanda Banquet |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Anupam Chattopadhyay, College of Computing & Data Science, NTU Singapore, Babak Hodjat, Cognizant, Balaji Thiagarajan, Flipkart, Hari Menon, Gates Foundation, Mike Haley, Autodesk, Raju Vegesna, Sify Technologies Ltd, Shereen Bhan, CNBC-TV18 |
| ü§ù **Partners** | Primus Partners |
| üé• **Video** | [‚ñ∂Ô∏è Watch on YouTube](https://youtube.com/live/RW9vl6Froqw?feature=share) |

> For India and the Global South, as AI systems move from pilots to mission-critical deployment across enterprises and governments, this challenge is amplified by fragmented and heterogeneous data, legacy IT infrastructure, uneven regulatory maturity, multilingual and culturally diverse populations, and high-impact use cases in finance, healthcare, welfare delivery, and public services.. This session will examine what enterprise-grade responsible AI looks like in such contexts, grounded in real deployments rather than abstract frameworks.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

For India and the Global South, as AI systems move from pilots to mission-critical deployment across enterprises and governments, this challenge is amplified by fragmented and heterogeneous data, legacy IT infrastructure, uneven regulatory maturity, multilingual and culturally diverse populations, and high-impact use cases in finance, healthcare, welfare delivery, and public services. This session will examine what enterprise-grade responsible AI looks like in such contexts, grounded in real deployments rather than abstract frameworks.

</details>

## 683. The 360¬∞ AI Stack: Scaling Intelligence through Infrastructure, Investment, and Integrity

| | |
|---|---|
| ‚è∞ **Time** | 17:30 ‚Äì 18:30 |
| üìç **Venue** | Bharat Mandapam | L1 Meeting Room 9 |
| üé§ **Speakers** | Dr. Taraknath Woddi, Annica Data Science, Mr. Paolo Benanti, Vatican |
| ü§ù **Partners** | IndiaAI |

> This panel presents a practical, cross-sector blueprint for scaling artificial intelligence by aligning technical capabilities, capital allocation, legal frameworks and infrastructure.. Panelists will examine how robust data engineering and production-grade model pipelines translate into investable business models, how investors filter technical promise from sustainable economics, and how legal and policy regimes for data and intellectual property shape commercialisation pathways.

<details>
<summary>üìñ Full Description</summary>

This panel presents a practical, cross-sector blueprint for scaling artificial intelligence by aligning technical capabilities, capital allocation, legal frameworks and infrastructure. Panelists will examine how robust data engineering and production-grade model pipelines translate into investable business models, how investors filter technical promise from sustainable economics, and how legal and policy regimes for data and intellectual property shape commercialisation pathways. The discussion brings together operator, investor, legal and infrastructure perspectives to surface concrete steps that synchronise funding rounds, regulatory compliance and platform upgrades for durable AI scale-up.

</details>
